<div data-bbox="64 185 529 196" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES) AND WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS) CONSENT</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 202 881 222" data-label="Text"><p>This consent form can only be used for whole exome sequencing and whole genome sequencing. Consent forms for other tests are located at Baylor Genetics' website (<a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/</a>).</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 226 851 237" data-label="Text"><p>For the purposes of this consent, "I", "my", "you", and "your" can refer to you, your child, your unborn child, or other individual you are the legal representative of.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 248 173 259" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>TEST INFORMATION</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 265 923 312" data-label="Text"><p>Your healthcare provider (doctor, genetic counselor, or other person with medical training) wants to order a genetic test called Whole Genome Sequencing (WGS) or Whole Exome Sequencing (WES). These tests look for changes, called variants, in a person's DNA that can cause health issues. DNA is our genetic material. These variants can be in certain genes, specific parts of our DNA that are needed for our health. They can also be found in other places in the genome (all DNA that a person has). Based on your known health issues, variants in your DNA that may cause these issues will be reported. This test may explain your health issues. It may also explain health issues that your family may have. Even if this test finds the cause of your health issues, this may not help treat or manage those issues.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 315 935 335" data-label="Text"><p>Testing where your DNA is compared to one or more family members may be performed. This may help better understand your results or show if your family members have the same variant as you.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 339 849 351" data-label="Text"><p>Before you sign this consent form, you should speak with your healthcare provider. They can help you understand this testing and what it means for your health.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 360 146 372" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>TEST RESULTS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 379 410 390" data-label="Text"><p>There are several types of test results that may be reported including:</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 394 933 514" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• <b>Positive:</b> A variant in the DNA was found that is related to your health issues or a health issue that you are at an increased risk of having in the future. These changes that cause disease are also known as pathogenic variants.</li>
<li>• <b>Negative:</b> No variants in the DNA were found that are related to your health issues or that would increase your risk of a health issue in the future.</li>
<li>• <b>Variant of Uncertain Clinical Significance (VUS):</b> A variant in the DNA was found that we do not know its effect, if any, on health. More testing may be needed for you or your family if a VUS is found that may be associated with your health issues.</li>
<li>• <b>Secondary and Incidental Findings (Optional):</b> Testing can sometimes find a variant in the DNA not related to the reason for testing but can change your medical care. <b>Note:</b> Certain issues within the brain start in adulthood and get worse over time (neurodegenerative). They often have no cure or treatment. By default, these variants will not be reported unless they are related to your health issues. However, variants in one or more of these gene(s) can be requested if needed. Your provider must write each gene needed in your test order.</li>
<li>• <b>Genes of No Known Disease Association (Optional):</b> Testing may find a variant in a gene that is not known to cause disease. This may be helpful to learn more about these genes in the future. These results do not currently impact medical management or indicate a diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="64 524 278 536" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>SECONDARY AND INCIDENTAL FINDINGS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 542 917 562" data-label="Text"><p>The following categories of variants are not expected to cause your current health issues. However, they can each be requested to be reported. Knowing about these variants might affect your future medical care.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 565 930 600" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• <b>ACMG Secondary Findings:</b> The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) recommends reporting disease-causing variants in certain genes that cause health issues. Each family member can request this group of variants to be reported.</li>
<li>• <b>Incidental Findings:</b> Other variants known to cause health issues but that are not causing your current health issues.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="64 610 258 622" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>CONSIDERATIONS AND LIMITATIONS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 628 908 740" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• You should speak with your provider before signing this consent form to understand the risks, benefits, and alternatives to testing.</li>
<li>• Testing may show you have, or are at increased chance of having, a health issue. It may show that you have an increased chance of having a child with a health issue.</li>
<li>• Even if the variant(s) causing your health issues are found, how these issues might progress or improve with treatment might not be known. Affected family members with the same variant might not be affected like you are.</li>
<li>• Depending on the results of testing, more testing may be needed to understand these results. This testing might be needed for you and/or other family members.</li>
<li>• A negative result does not rule out the chance for health issues. Our knowledge of variants and how they cause disease may change over time as we learn more about genetics. Testing has limitations to what it can find as well.</li>
<li>• Certain factors may lead to incorrect results. These include mislabeled samples, incorrect information in the test order, and rare technical errors.</li>
<li>• More sample may be needed from you if the first sample is not sufficient to complete testing.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="64 750 366 761" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>USE OF DATA AND SPECIMEN FOR RESEARCH PURPOSES</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 767 929 806" data-label="Text"><p>Biological specimens, test results, and associated information may be used by Baylor Genetics and its research partners for anonymous or coded research purposes, including improving genetic testing, advancing knowledge of genetic conditions, and developing new technologies, including inclusion in de-identified clinical databases, only with the patient's informed consent. Patient data and specimen will not be used for anonymous or coded research, unless authorized by marking below. A patient's decision to decline participation shall not affect their ability to receive testing from Baylor Genetics.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 809 599 821" data-label="Text"><p>For Oregon patients, please consult the state specific consent form found at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/forms">www.baylorgenetics.com/forms</a>.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="64 821 494 835" data-label="List-Group">
<p><input checked="" type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics the use of my specimen and de-identified data for research.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 846 333 857" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>FOR SAMPLES FROM NEW YORK STATE RESIDENTS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="61 862 910 884" data-label="Text"><p>Samples from New York State residents shall not be included in research without written consent. Samples will not be retained for more than sixty (60) days after receipt by Baylor Genetics, unless authorized by marking below. No tests other than those authorized shall be performed on the samples.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="61 885 802 898" data-label="List-Group"><p><input type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics to retain sample(s) longer based on our retention policy for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes.</p></div>

<div data-bbox="70 188 354 201" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 206 937 250" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• If several family members are tested, knowing the correct biological relationships among them is important. In rare cases, testing can show that family members are not related as expected. If this is found, we may contact the provider who ordered your testing.</li>
<li>• If this testing is requested to be cancelled after the order and sample are sent to the laboratory, please see our Test Cancellation Policy at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/">www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 260 427 273" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION (CONTINUED)</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 277 939 457" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• Only Baylor Genetics and its contracted partners will have access to your sample for the ordered testing. Results from testing will only be released to: (i) a licensed healthcare provider, (ii) those authorized in writing, (iii) the patient or their personal representative, and (iv) those allowed access to test results by law. You have the right to access your test results from Baylor Genetics by providing a written request. You also have the right to request raw data obtained from your sample by providing a written request or HIPAA Authorization Form.</li>
<li>• In rare cases, people with genetic diseases may have problems with health insurance and employment. The U.S. Federal Government has several laws that prohibit discrimination based on test results by health insurance companies and employers. These laws also prohibit unauthorized disclosure of this information. For more information, please visit <a href="http://www.genome.gov/10092077">www.genome.gov/10092077</a>.</li>
<li>• Samples will be kept in the laboratory based on our retention policy. Once testing is completed, the de-identified sample may be used for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes. Samples are not returned to patients or providers unless requested prior to testing. You and your heirs will not receive payments, benefits, or rights to any resulting products or discoveries.</li>
<li>• The information from your testing may be used in scientific research, publications or presentations, but your specific identity will not be revealed. We may contact your provider to obtain more clinical information about you. Baylor Genetics also performs other types of scientific research and may contact you to see if you would like to be involved.</li>
<li>• Variants found may be submitted to databases. The medical community uses these databases to collect information about how variants might cause disease to improve testing and treatment for patients. An example is ClinVar, a free, public archive of reports on human genetics. Limited clinical information may need to be shared with these databases. In rare cases, this information may be enough to allow you or your family members to be identified.</li>
<li>• For more information on privacy practices at Baylor Genetics, please visit <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/">www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div data-bbox="66 203 935 255" data-label="Text"><p>This requisition hereby incorporates the Terms and Conditions of the Laboratory Services found at <a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/lab-terms-conditions/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/lab-terms-conditions/</a> or, in the case of international entities, <a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/terms-conditions-of-the-laboratory-services-international/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/terms-conditions-of-the-laboratory-services-international/</a>. <div style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 2px; font-weight: bold; margin-top: 10px;">INSTRUCTIONS FOR ORDERING</div>
<div data-bbox="66 330 895 352" data-label="Text"><p>Familial samples are <b>required</b> for non-<i>Proband</i> WGS. Please contact the laboratory if placing a test order where the comparator(s) are different than the required family members listed.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="66 357 932 410" data-label="Text"><p>For select cases when appropriate as determined by Baylor Genetics, WGS may be supplemented by RNA-Seq and/or Optical Genome Mapping (OGM)* to aid with variant classification and/or result clarification as a standard part of this test offering. If the originally submitted specimen is blood and meets all established specimen requirements, RNA-Seq and/or OGM will be reflexively performed without additional authorization. If these requirements are not met, submission of a new blood specimen may be requested, or reflexive testing may not be performed. A final report will be issued prior to initiating RNA-Seq and/or OGM. Any updates resulting from these additional technologies will be provided through an addended report. Additionally, Long-Read Sequencing (LRS) may be used to confirm certain results.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="66 413 547 423" data-label="Footnote"><p>*OGM and LRS have not yet been approved in New York state and will not be performed on specimens collected there.</p></div>

In rare cases, testing can show that family members are not related as expected. If this is found, we may contact the provider who ordered your testing.</li><li>• If this testing is requested to be cancelled after the order and sample are sent to the laboratory, please see our Test Cancellation Policy at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/">www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/</a>.</li></ul></div><div data-bbox="64 259 419 270" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION (CONTINUED)</b></p></div><div data-bbox="64 275 933 456" data-label="List-Group"><ul><li>• Only Baylor Genetics and its contracted partners will have access to your sample for the ordered testing. Results from testing will only be released to: (i) a licensed healthcare provider, (ii) those authorized in writing, (iii) the patient or their personal representative, and (iv) those allowed access to test results by law. You have the right to access your test results from Baylor Genetics by providing a written request. You also have the right to request raw data obtained from your sample by providing a written request or HIPAA Authorization Form.</li><li>• In rare cases, people with genetic diseases may have problems with health insurance and employment. The U.S. Federal Government has several laws that prohibit discrimination based on test results by health insurance companies and employers. These laws also prohibit unauthorized disclosure of this information. For more information, please visit <a href="http://www.genome.gov/10002077">www.genome.gov/10002077</a>.</li><li>• Samples will be kept in the laboratory based on our retention policy. Once testing is completed, the de-identified sample may be used for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes. Samples are not returned to patients or providers unless requested prior to testing. You and your heirs will not receive payments, benefits, or rights to any resulting products or discoveries.</li><li>• The information from your testing may be used in scientific research, publications or presentations, but your specific identity will not be revealed. We may contact your provider to obtain more clinical information about you. Baylor Genetics also performs other types of scientific research and may contact you to see if you would like to be involved.</li><li>• Variants found may be submitted to databases. The medical community uses these databases to collect information about how variants might cause disease to improve testing and treatment for patients. An example is ClinVar, a free, public archive of reports on human genetics. Limited clinical information may need to be shared with these databases. In rare cases, this information may be enough to allow you or your family members to be identified.</li><li>• For more information on privacy practices at Baylor Genetics, please visit <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/">www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/</a>.</li></ul></div><div data-bbox="64 468 194 480" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>FINANCIAL AGREEMENT</b></p></div><div data-bbox="64 484 930 524" data-label="Text"><p>By signing below, I hereby authorize Baylor Genetics to provide my insurance carrier any information necessary, including test results, for processing my insurance claim. I designate Baylor Genetics as my designated representative for purposes of appealing any denial of benefits by my insurance carrier. I irrevocably assign associated payment to Baylor Genetics, and direct that payment be made directly to Baylor Genetics. <div data-bbox="67 187 534 199" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES) AND WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS) CONSENT</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="67 204 884 224" data-label="Text"><p>This consent form can only be used for whole exome sequencing and whole genome sequencing. Consent forms for other tests are located at Baylor Genetics' website (<a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/</a>).</p></div>
<div data-bbox="67 228 854 241" data-label="Text"><p>For the purposes of this consent, "I", "my", "you", and "your" can refer to you, your child, your unborn child, or other individual you are the legal representative of.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="67 249 177 260" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>TEST INFORMATION</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 266 923 317" data-label="Text"><p>Your healthcare provider (doctor, genetic counselor, or other person with medical training) wants to order a genetic test called Whole Genome Sequencing (WGS) or Whole Exome Sequencing (WES). These tests look for changes, called variants, in a person's DNA that can cause health issues. DNA is our genetic material. These variants can be in certain genes, specific parts of our DNA that are needed for our health. They can also be found in other places in the genome (all DNA that a person has). Based on your known health issues, variants in your DNA that may cause these issues will be reported. This test may explain your health issues. It may also explain health issues that your family may have. Even if this test finds the cause of your health issues, this may not help treat or manage those issues.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 316 933 337" data-label="Text"><p>Testing where your DNA is compared to one or more family members may be performed. This may help better understand your results or show if your family members have the same variant as you.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 341 851 355" data-label="Text"><p>Before you sign this consent form, you should speak with your healthcare provider. They can help you understand this testing and what it means for your health.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 362 150 374" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>TEST RESULTS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 380 415 393" data-label="Text"><p>There are several types of test results that may be reported including:</p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 395 931 518" data-label="List-Group">
<ul style="list-style-type: none;">
<li>• <b>Positive:</b> A variant in the DNA was found that is related to your health issues or a health issue that you are at an increased risk of having in the future. These changes that cause disease are also known as pathogenic variants.</li>
<li>• <b>Negative:</b> No variants in the DNA were found that are related to your health issues or that would increase your risk of a health issue in the future.</li>
<li>• <b>Variant of Uncertain Clinical Significance (VUS):</b> A variant in the DNA was found that we do not know its effect, if any, on health. More testing may be needed for you or your family if a VUS is found that may be associated with your health issues.</li>
<li>• <b>Secondary and Incidental Findings (Optional):</b> Testing can sometimes find a variant in the DNA not related to the reason for testing but can change your medical care.<br/><b>Note:</b> Certain issues within the brain start in adulthood and get worse over time (neurodegenerative). They often have no cure or treatment. By default, these variants will not be reported unless they are related to your health issues. However, variants in one or more of these gene(s) can be requested if needed. Your provider must write each gene needed in your test order.</li>
<li>• <b>Genes of No Known Disease Association (Optional):</b> Testing may find a variant in a gene that is not known to cause disease. This may be helpful to learn more about these genes in the future. These results do not currently impact medical management or indicate a diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 525 283 538" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>SECONDARY AND INCIDENTAL FINDINGS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 543 915 563" data-label="Text"><p>The following categories of variants are not expected to cause your current health issues. However, they can each be requested to be reported. Knowing about these variants might affect your future medical care.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 566 928 602" data-label="List-Group">
<ul style="list-style-type: none;">
<li>• <b>ACMG Secondary Findings:</b> The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) recommends reporting disease-causing variants in certain genes that cause health issues. Each family member can request this group of variants to be reported.</li>
<li>• <b>Incidental Findings:</b> Other variants known to cause health issues but that are not causing your current health issues.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 611 260 625" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>CONSIDERATIONS AND LIMITATIONS</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="65 629 908 743" data-label="List-Group">
<ul style="list-style-type: none;">
<li>• You should speak with your provider before signing this consent form to understand the risks, benefits, and alternatives to testing.</li>
<li>• Testing may show you have, or are at increased chance of having, a health issue. It may show that you have an increased chance of having a child with a health issue.</li>
<li>• Even if the variant(s) causing your health issues are found, how these issues might progress or improve with treatment might not be known. Affected family members with the same variant might not be affected like you are.</li>
<li>• Depending on the results of testing, more testing may be needed to understand these results. This testing might be needed for you and/or other family members.</li>
<li>• A negative result does not rule out the chance for health issues. Our knowledge of variants and how they cause disease may change over time as we learn more about genetics. Testing has limitations to what it can find as well.</li>
<li>• Certain factors may lead to incorrect results. These include mislabeled samples, incorrect information in the test order, and rare technical errors.</li>
<li>• More sample may be needed from you if the first sample is not sufficient to complete testing.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 751 368 764" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>USE OF DATA AND SPECIMEN FOR RESEARCH PURPOSES</b></p></div>
<div data-bbox="63 768 926 809" data-label="Text"><p>Biological specimens, test results, and associated information may be used by Baylor Genetics and its research partners for anonymous or coded research purposes, including improving genetic testing, advancing knowledge of genetic conditions, and developing new technologies, including inclusion in de-identified clinical databases, only with the patient's informed consent. Patient data and specimen will not be used for anonymous or coded research, unless authorized by marking below. A patient's decision to decline participation shall not affect their ability to receive testing from Baylor Genetics.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="63 811 599 825" data-label="Text"><p>For Oregon patients, please consult the state specific consent form found at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/forms">www.baylorgenetics.com/forms</a>.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="63 823 760 850" data-label="Text"><p><input type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics the use of my specimen and de-identified data for research <i>[signature]</i></p></div>
<div data-bbox="63 848 335 860" data-label="Section-Header"><p><b>FOR SAMPLES FROM NEW YORK STATE RESIDENTS</b></p></div>

Samples will not be retained for more than sixty (60) days after receipt by Baylor Genetics, unless authorized by marking below. No tests other than those authorized shall be performed on the samples.</p></div>

The results of MCC studies are not used for the treatment or management of the fetus, pregnant person, or other individuals, and are not part of the pregnant person's designated medical record.</p>

<div data-bbox="69 296 234 309" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>INSTRUCTIONS FOR ORDERING</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="66 312 894 335" data-label="Text">
<p>Familial samples are required for non-Proband WES. Please contact the laboratory if placing a test order where the comparator(s) are different than the required family members listed.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="66 339 905 383" data-label="Text">
<p>For select cases as determined by Baylor Genetics, WES may be supplemented by RNA-Seq to aid with variant classification as a standard part of this test offering. If the originally submitted specimen is blood and meets all established specimen requirements, RNA-Seq will be reflexively performed without additional authorization. If these requirements are not met, submission of a new blood specimen may be requested, or reflexive testing may not be performed. A final report will be issued prior to initiating RNA-Seq. Any updates resulting from this additional technology will be provided through an addendum report.</p>
</div>

    </p>

<div data-bbox="61 183 529 195" data-label="Section-Header">
<h3>WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES) AND WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS) CONSENT</h3>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 199 879 221" data-label="Text">
<p>This consent form can only be used for whole exome sequencing and whole genome sequencing. Consent forms for other tests are located at Baylor Genetics' website (<a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/</a>).</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 224 850 237" data-label="Text">
<p>For the purposes of this consent, "I", "my", "you", and "your" can refer to you, your child, your unborn child, or other individual you are the legal representative of.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 246 173 259" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>TEST INFORMATION</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 263 917 313" data-label="Text">
<p>Your healthcare provider (doctor, genetic counselor, or other person with medical training) wants to order a genetic test called Whole Genome Sequencing (WGS) or Whole Exome Sequencing (WES). These tests look for changes, called variants, in a person's DNA that can cause health issues. DNA is our genetic material. These variants can be in certain genes, specific parts of our DNA that are needed for our health. They can also be found in other places in the genome (all DNA that a person has). Based on your known health issues, variants in your DNA that may cause these issues will be reported. This test may explain your health issues. It may also explain health issues that your family may have. Even if this test finds the cause of your health issues, this may not help treat or manage those issues.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 313 927 335" data-label="Text">
<p>Testing where your DNA is compared to one or more family members may be performed. This may help better understand your results or show if your family members have the same variant as you.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 337 847 350" data-label="Text">
<p>Before you sign this consent form, you should speak with your healthcare provider. They can help you understand this testing and what it means for your health.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 360 148 373" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>TEST RESULTS</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 377 411 390" data-label="Text">
<p>There are several types of test results that may be reported including:</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 392 928 514" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• <b>Positive:</b> A variant in the DNA was found that is related to your health issues or a health issue that you are at an increased risk of having in the future. These changes that cause disease are also known as pathogenic variants.</li>
<li>• <b>Negative:</b> No variants in the DNA were found that are related to your health issues or that would increase your risk of a health issue in the future.</li>
<li>• <b>Variant of Uncertain Clinical Significance (VUS):</b> A variant in the DNA was found that we do not know its effect, if any, on health. More testing may be needed for you or your family if a VUS is found that may be associated with your health issues.</li>
<li>• <b>Secondary and Incidental Findings (Optional):</b> Testing can sometimes find a variant in the DNA not related to the reason for testing but can change your medical care. <b>Note:</b> Certain issues within the brain start in adulthood and get worse over time (neurodegenerative). They often have no cure or treatment. By default, these variants will not be reported unless they are related to your health issues. However, variants in one or more of these gene(s) can be requested if needed. Your provider must write each gene needed in your test order.</li>
<li>• <b>Genes of No Known Disease Association (Optional):</b> Testing may find a variant in a gene that is not known to cause disease. This may be helpful to learn more about these genes in the future. These results do not currently impact medical management or indicate a diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 523 280 535" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>SECONDARY AND INCIDENTAL FINDINGS</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 540 913 562" data-label="Text">
<p>The following categories of variants are not expected to cause your current health issues. However, they can each be requested to be reported. Knowing about these variants might affect your future medical care.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 564 926 601" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• <b>ACMG Secondary Findings:</b> The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) recommends reporting disease-causing variants in certain genes that cause health issues. Each family member can request this group of variants to be reported.</li>
<li>• <b>Incidental Findings:</b> Other variants known to cause health issues but that are not causing your current health issues.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 610 259 624" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>CONSIDERATIONS AND LIMITATIONS</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 627 904 740" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• You should speak with your provider before signing this consent form to understand the risks, benefits, and alternatives to testing.</li>
<li>• Testing may show you have, or are at increased chance of having, a health issue. It may show that you have an increased chance of having a child with a health issue.</li>
<li>• Even if the variant(s) causing your health issues are found, how these issues might progress or improve with treatment might not be known. Affected family members with the same variant might not be affected like you are.</li>
<li>• Depending on the results of testing, more testing may be needed to understand these results. This testing might be needed for you and/or other family members.</li>
<li>• A negative result does not rule out the chance for health issues. Our knowledge of variants and how they cause disease may change over time as we learn more about genetics. Testing has limitations to what it can find as well.</li>
<li>• Certain factors may lead to incorrect results. These include mislabeled samples, incorrect information in the test order, and rare technical errors.</li>
<li>• More sample may be needed from you if the first sample is not sufficient to complete testing.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 750 367 763" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>USE OF DATA AND SPECIMEN FOR RESEARCH PURPOSES</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 767 923 807" data-label="Text">
<p>Biological specimens, test results, and associated information may be used by Baylor Genetics and its research partners for anonymous or coded research purposes, including improving genetic testing, advancing knowledge of genetic conditions, and developing new technologies, including inclusion in de-identified clinical databases, only with the patient's informed consent. Patient data and specimen will not be used for anonymous or coded research, unless authorized by marking below. A patient's decision to decline participation shall not affect their ability to receive testing from Baylor Genetics.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 809 599 822" data-label="Text">
<p><input checked="" type="checkbox"/> For Oregon patients, please consult the state specific consent form found at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/forms">www.baylorgenetics.com/forms</a>.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 822 497 836" data-label="Text">
<p><input type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics the use of my specimen and de-identified data for research.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 846 333 859" data-label="Section-Header">
<h4>FOR SAMPLES FROM NEW YORK STATE RESIDENTS</h4>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 863 907 884" data-label="Text">
<p>Samples from New York State residents shall not be included in research without written consent. Samples will not be retained for more than sixty (60) days after receipt by Baylor Genetics, unless authorized by marking below. No tests other than those authorized shall be performed on the samples.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 885 802 900" data-label="Text">
<p><input type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics to retain sample(s) longer based on our retention policy for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes.</p>
</div>

<div data-bbox="67 188 354 200" data-label="Section-Header"><h4>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION</h4></div>
<div data-bbox="67 204 930 247" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• If several family members are tested, knowing the correct biological relationships among them is important. In rare cases, testing can show that family members are not related as expected. If this is found, we may contact the provider who ordered your testing.</li>
<li>• If this testing is requested to be cancelled after the order and sample are sent to the laboratory, please see our Test Cancellation Policy at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/">www.baylorgenetics.com/cancel-test/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="67 258 427 271" data-label="Section-Header"><h4>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION (CONTINUED)</h4></div>
<div data-bbox="67 275 932 458" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>• Only Baylor Genetics and its contracted partners will have access to your sample for the ordered testing. Results from testing will only be released to: (i) a licensed healthcare provider, (ii) those authorized in writing, (iii) the patient or their personal representative, and (iv) those allowed access to test results by law. You have the right to access your test results from Baylor Genetics by providing a written request. You also have the right to request raw data obtained from your sample by providing a written request or HIPAA Authorization Form.</li>
<li>• In rare cases, people with genetic diseases may have problems with health insurance and employment. The U.S. Federal Government has several laws that prohibit discrimination based on test results by health insurance companies and employers. These laws also prohibit unauthorized disclosure of this information. For more information, please visit <a href="http://www.genome.gov/10002077">www.genome.gov/10002077</a>.</li>
<li>• Samples will be kept in the laboratory based on our retention policy. Once testing is completed, the de-identified sample may be used for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes. Samples are not returned to patients or providers unless requested prior to testing. You and your heirs will not receive payments, benefits, or rights to any resulting products or discoveries.</li>
<li>• The information from your testing may be used in scientific research, publications or presentations, but your specific identity will not be revealed. We may contact your provider to obtain more clinical information about you. Baylor Genetics also performs other types of scientific research and may contact you to see if you would like to be involved.</li>
<li>• Variants found may be submitted to databases. The medical community uses these databases to collect information about how variants might cause disease to improve testing and treatment for patients. An example is ClinVar, a free, public archive of reports on human genetics. Limited clinical information may need to be shared with these databases. In rare cases, this information may be enough to allow you or your family members to be identified.</li>
<li>• For more information on privacy practices at Baylor Genetics, please visit <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/">www.baylorgenetics.com/privacy-practices/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>

I understand that I am responsible for any co-pay, co-insurance, and unmet deductible that the insurance policy dictates. I designate Baylor Genetics as my designated representative for purposes of appealing any denial of benefits by my insurance carrier. I irrevocably assign associated payment to Baylor Genetics, and direct that payment be made directly to Baylor Genetics. Please note, some payers may not cover certain screening tests.</p></div>
<div data-bbox="67 528 929 560" data-label="Text"><p>If my health insurer does not cover the test or I do not have health insurance, I have received a good faith estimate of the cost for the genetic testing ordered by my provider and agree to pay for the cost of the genetic testing billed to me by Baylor Genetics based on that good faith estimate. More information is available in Baylor Genetics' No Surprises Act and Good Faith Estimate Notice located at <a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/no-surprises-act/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/no-surprises-act/</a>.</p></div>

<p><b>WHAT YOU NEED TO DO NOW:</b></p>
</div>

<li>• Choose an option below about whether to receive the <b>Baylor Genetics test</b> listed above.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 570 911 597" data-label="Text">
<p>Note: If you choose Option 1 or 2, we may help you to use any other insurance that you might have, but Medicare cannot require us to do this.</p>

<b>STATEMENT OF MEDICAL NECESSITY AND CONSENT TO TERMS &amp; CONDITIONS FOR TEST ORDER (REQUIRED)</b>
</div>
<p><small>This requisition hereby incorporates the Terms and Conditions of the Laboratory Services found at <a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/lab-terms-conditions/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/lab-terms-conditions/</a> or, in the case of international entities, <a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/terms-conditions-of-the-laboratory-services-international/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/terms-conditions-of-the-laboratory-services-international/</a>. This test is medically necessary for the risk assessment, diagnosis, or detection of a disease, illness, impairment, symptom, syndrome, or disorder. The results will determine my patient's medical management and treatment decisions. The person listed as the Ordering Physician is authorized by law to order the test(s) requested herein. I confirm that I have provided genetic testing information to the patient, and they have consented to genetic testing.</small></p>

<div style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 5px; margin-top: 20px; font-size: 0.85em;">
<b>INSTRUCTIONS FOR ORDERING</b>
</div>
<p><small>Familial samples are required for non-Proband WGS. Please contact the laboratory if placing a test order where the comparator(s) are different than the required family members listed.</small></p>
<p><small>For select cases when appropriate as determined by Baylor Genetics, WGS may be supplemented by RNA-Seq and/or Optical Genome Mapping (OGM)* to aid with variant classification and/or result clarification as a standard part of this test offering. If the originally submitted specimen is blood and meets all established specimen requirements, RNA-Seq and/or OGM will be reflexively performed without additional authorization. If these requirements are not met, submission of a new blood specimen may be requested, or reflexive testing may not be performed. A final report will be issued prior to initiating RNA-Seq and/or OGM. Any updates resulting from these additional technologies will be provided through an addendum. Additionally, Long-Read Sequencing (LRS) may be used to confirm certain results.</small></p>
<p><small>*OGM and LRS have not yet been approved in New York state and will not be performed on specimens collected there.</small></p>

<div data-bbox="63 120 542 133" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>INFORMED CONSENT FOR WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS)</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 132 870 143" data-label="Text">
<p>For the purposes of this consent, "you", "me", "my", and "I" can also mean your child (including unborn child) or the individual you are the personal representative for.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 134 921 174" data-label="Text">
<p>
    Patient Last Name <u>Carson</u> Patient First Name <u>Henry</u> MI <u></u> Date of Birth (MM / DD / YYYY) <u>01 / 01 / 1992</u> Genetic Sex <u>M</u>
</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 183 528 194" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES) AND WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS) CONSENT</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 200 877 220" data-label="Text">
<p>This consent form can only be used for whole exome sequencing and whole genome sequencing. Consent forms for other tests are located at Baylor Genetics' website (<a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/</a>).</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 224 847 234" data-label="Text">
<p>For the purposes of this consent, "I", "my", "you", and "your" can refer to you, your child, your unborn child, or other individual you are the legal representative of.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 245 195 257" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>TEST INFORMATION</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 263 915 311" data-label="Text">
<p>Your healthcare provider (doctor, genetic counselor, or other person with medical training) wants to order a genetic test called Whole Genome Sequencing (WGS) or Whole Exome Sequencing (WES). These tests look for changes, called variants, in a person's DNA that can cause health issues. DNA is our genetic material. These variants can be in certain genes, specific parts of our DNA that are needed for our health. They can also be found in other places in the genome (all DNA that a person has). Based on your known health issues, variants in your DNA that may cause these issues will be reported. This test may explain your health issues. It may also explain health issues that your family may have. Even if this test finds the cause of your health issues, this may not help treat or manage those issues.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 311 925 333" data-label="Text">
<p>Testing where your DNA is compared to one or more family members may be performed. This may help better understand your results or show if your family members have the same variant as you.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 336 925 348" data-label="Text">
<p>Before you sign this consent form, you should speak with your healthcare provider. They can help you understand this testing and what it means for your health.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 358 175 370" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>TEST RESULTS</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 376 515 387" data-label="Text">
<p>There are several types of test results that may be reported including:</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 391 921 513" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li><strong>Positive:</strong> A variant in the DNA was found that is related to your health issues or a health issue that you are at an increased risk of having in the future. These changes that cause disease are also known as pathogenic variants.</li>
<li><strong>Negative:</strong> No variants in the DNA were found that are related to your health issues or that would increase your risk of a health issue in the future.</li>
<li><strong>Variant of Uncertain Clinical Significance (VUS):</strong> A variant in the DNA was found that we do not know its effect, if any, on health. More testing may be needed for you or your family if a VUS is found that may be associated with your health issues.</li>
<li><strong>Secondary and Incidental Findings (Optional):</strong> Testing can sometimes find a variant in the DNA not related to the reason for testing but can change your medical care. <strong>Note:</strong> Certain issues within the brain start in adulthood and get worse over time (neurodegenerative). They often have no cure or treatment. By default, these variants will not be reported unless they are related to your health issues. However, variants in one or more of these gene(s) can be requested if needed. Your provider must write each gene needed in your test order.</li>
<li><strong>Genes of No Known Disease Association (Optional):</strong> Testing may find a variant in a gene that is not known to cause disease. This may be helpful to learn more about these genes in the future. These results do not currently impact medical management or indicate a diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 523 280 534" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>SECONDARY AND INCIDENTAL FINDINGS</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 540 921 561" data-label="Text">
<p>The following categories of variants are not expected to cause your current health issues. However, they can each be requested to be reported. Knowing about these variants might affect your future medical care.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 565 921 598" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li><strong>ACMG Secondary Findings:</strong> The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) recommends reporting disease-causing variants in certain genes that cause health issues. Each family member can request this group of variants to be reported.</li>
<li><strong>Incidental Findings:</strong> Other variants known to cause health issues but that are not causing your current health issues.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 610 260 621" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>CONSIDERATIONS AND LIMITATIONS</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 628 921 739" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>You should speak with your provider before signing this consent form to understand the risks, benefits, and alternatives to testing.</li>
<li>Testing may show you have, or are at increased chance of having, a health issue. It may show that you have an increased chance of having a child with a health issue.</li>
<li>Even if the variant(s) causing your health issues are found, how these issues might progress or improve with treatment might not be known. Affected family members with the same variant might not be affected like you are.</li>
<li>Depending on the results of testing, more testing may be needed to understand these results. This testing might be needed for you and/or other family members.</li>
<li>A negative result does not rule out the chance for health issues. Our knowledge of variants and how they cause disease may change over time as we learn more about genetics. Testing has limitations to what it can find as well.</li>
<li>Certain factors may lead to incorrect results. These include mislabeled samples, incorrect information in the test order, and rare technical errors.</li>
<li>More sample may be needed from you if the first sample is not sufficient to complete testing.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 749 390 761" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>USE OF DATA AND SPECIMEN FOR RESEARCH PURPOSES</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 766 921 804" data-label="Text">
<p>Biological specimens, test results, and associated information may be used by Baylor Genetics and its research partners for anonymous or coded research purposes, including improving genetic testing, advancing knowledge of genetic conditions, and developing new technologies, including inclusion in de-identified clinical databases, only with the patient's informed consent. Patient data and specimen will not be used for anonymous or coded research, unless authorized by marking below. A patient's decision to decline participation shall not affect their ability to receive testing from Baylor Genetics.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="15 820 600 834" data-label="Text">
<p>For Oregon patients, please consult the state specific consent form found at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/forms">www.baylorgenetics.com/forms</a>.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 823 495 834" data-label="Text">
<p><input checked="" type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics the use of my specimen and de-identified data for research.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 845 345 856" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><strong>FOR SAMPLES FROM NEW YORK STATE RESIDENTS</strong></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 861 921 883" data-label="Text">
<p>Samples from New York State residents shall not be included in research without written consent. Samples will not be retained for more than sixty (60) days after receipt by Baylor Genetics, unless authorized by marking below. No tests other than those authorized shall be performed on the samples.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="63 887 796 897" data-label="Text">
<p><input checked="" type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics to retain sample(s) longer based on our retention policy for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes.</p>
</div>

<div data-bbox="70 189 354 201" data-label="Section-Header" style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 2px;">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 207 938 250" data-label="List-Group">
<ul style="list-style-type: none;">
<li>• If several family members are tested, knowing the correct biological relationships among them is important. In rare cases, testing can show that family members are not related as expected. If this is found, we may contact the provider who ordered your testing.</li>
<li>• If this testing is requested to be cancelled after the order and sample are sent to the laboratory, please see our Test Cancellation Policy at <a href="http://www.bayloregenetics.com/cancel-test/"><u>www.bayloregenetics.com/cancel-test/</u></a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 260 427 271" data-label="Section-Header" style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 2px;">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION (CONTINUED)</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 278 938 459" data-label="List-Group">
<ul style="list-style-type: none;">
<li>• Only Baylor Genetics and its contracted partners will have access to your sample for the ordered testing. Results from testing will only be released to: (i) a licensed healthcare provider, (ii) those authorized in writing, (iii) the patient or their personal representative, and (iv) those allowed access to test results by law. You have the right to access your test results from Baylor Genetics by providing a written request. You also have the right to request raw data obtained from your sample by providing a written request or HIPAA Authorization Form.</li>
<li>• In rare cases, people with genetic diseases may have problems with health insurance and employment. The U.S. Federal Government has several laws that prohibit discrimination based on test results by health insurance companies and employers. These laws also prohibit unauthorized disclosure of this information. For more information, please visit <a href="http://www.genome.gov/10002077"><u>www.genome.gov/10002077</u></a>.</li>
<li>• Samples will be kept in the laboratory based on our retention policy. Once testing is completed, the de-identified sample may be used for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes. Samples are not returned to patients or providers unless requested prior to testing. You and your heirs will not receive payments, benefits, or rights to any resulting products or discoveries.</li>
<li>• The information from your testing may be used in scientific research, publications or presentations, but your specific identity will not be revealed. We may contact your provider to obtain more clinical information about you. Baylor Genetics also performs other types of scientific research and may contact you to see if you would like to be involved.</li>
<li>• Variants found may be submitted to databases. The medical community uses these databases to collect information about how variants might cause disease to improve testing and treatment for patients. An example is ClinVar, a free, public archive of reports on human genetics. Limited clinical information may need to be shared with these databases. In rare cases, this information may be enough to allow you or your family members to be identified.</li>
<li>• For more information on privacy practices at Baylor Genetics, please visit <a href="http://www.bayloregenetics.com/privacy-practices/"><u>www.bayloregenetics.com/privacy-practices/</u></a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 469 199 480" data-label="Section-Header" style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 2px;">
<p><b>FINANCIAL AGREEMENT</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 487 938 526" data-label="Text">
<p>By signing below, I hereby authorize Baylor Genetics to provide my insurance carrier any information necessary, including test results, for processing my insurance claim. I understand that I am responsible for any co-pay, co-insurance, and unmet deductible that the insurance policy dictates. I designate Baylor Genetics as my designated representative for purposes of appealing any denial of benefits by my insurance carrier. I irrevocably assign associated payment to Baylor Genetics, and direct that payment be made directly to Baylor Genetics. Please note, some payers may not cover certain screening tests.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 528 938 559" data-label="Text">
<p>If my health insurer does not cover the test or I do not have health insurance, I have received a good faith estimate of the cost for the genetic testing ordered by my provider and agree to pay for the cost of the genetic testing billed to me by Baylor Genetics based on that good faith estimate. More information is available in Baylor Genetics' No Surprises Act and Good Faith Estimate Notice located at <a href="https://www.bayloregenetics.com/no-surprises-act/"><u>https://www.bayloregenetics.com/no-surprises-act/</u></a>.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 561 643 574" data-label="Text">
<p>A Medicare Advance Beneficiary Notice (ABN) is required for services Medicare identifies as not medically necessary.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 583 206 594" data-label="Section-Header" style="background-color: black; color: white; padding: 2px;">
<p><b>PATIENT AUTHORIZATION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 601 938 641" data-label="Text">
<p>By signing this statement of consent, I acknowledge that I have read, understand, and hereby grant my informed consent for genetic testing. I have received appropriate explanations from my healthcare provider about the planned genetic test(s) and possible results. I have been informed by my healthcare provider about the availability and importance of genetic counseling and have been provided with written information identifying a genetic counselor or medical geneticist who can provide such counseling services. All my questions have been answered, and I have had the necessary time to make an informed decision about the genetic test(s).</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 643 733 655" data-label="Text">
<p><b>Note:</b> If Prenatal WES was ordered, please leave the Patient section blank and complete only a section for each relative tested below.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="70 656 632 668" data-label="Text">
<p>I hereby give permission to Baylor Genetics to conduct genetic testing as recommended by my healthcare provider.*</p>

  Variants in genes included in the ACMG secondary findings guidelines will be reported for each family member marked below. Each marked family member will receive their own report on these findings.</p>

</div>
<div data-bbox="56 266 780 277" data-label="Text">

<div data-bbox="61 280 567 293" data-label="Text">

</div>
<div data-bbox="56 293 505 304" data-label="Section-Header">

</div>
<div data-bbox="56 303 598 314" data-label="Text">
<p>For variants in genes with no known disease association, these variants will be reported if biallelic or de novo.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="61 318 506 330" data-label="Text">
<p><input type="checkbox"/> Please report biallelic and de novo variants in genes with no known disease association.</p>

<p><b>INFORMED CONSENT FOR WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES)</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 132 871 149" data-label="Text">
<p>For the purposes of this consent, "you", "me", "my", and "I" can also mean your child (including unborn child) or the individual you are the personal representative for.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 162 866 175" data-label="Text">
<p>Patient Last Name: [Handwritten: <u>TACCO</u>] Patient First Name: [Handwritten: <u>FREDERICK</u>] MI: _____ Date of Birth (MM / DD / YYYY): [Handwritten: <u>03/13/2024</u>] Genetic Sex: [Handwritten: <u>U</u>]</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 184 529 196" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>WHOLE EXOME SEQUENCING (WES) AND WHOLE GENOME SEQUENCING (WGS) CONSENT</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 200 878 222" data-label="Text">
<p>This consent form can only be used for whole exome sequencing and whole genome sequencing. Consent forms for other tests are located at Baylor Genetics' website (<a href="https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/">https://www.baylorgenetics.com/consent/</a>).</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 225 850 238" data-label="Text">
<p>For the purposes of this consent, "I", "my", "you", and "your" can refer to you, your child, your unborn child, or other individual you are the legal representative of.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 248 174 260" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>TEST INFORMATION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 265 918 314" data-label="Text">
<p>Your healthcare provider (doctor, genetic counselor, or other person with medical training) wants to order a genetic test called <b>Whole Genome Sequencing (WGS)</b> or <b>Whole Exome Sequencing (WES)</b>. These tests look for changes, called variants, in a person's DNA that can cause health issues. DNA is our genetic material. These variants can be in certain genes, specific parts of our DNA that are needed for our health. They can also be found in other places in the genome (all DNA that a person has). Based on your known health issues, variants in your DNA that may cause these issues will be reported. This test may explain your health issues. It may also explain health issues that your family may have. Even if this test finds the cause of your health issues, this may not help treat or manage those issues.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 315 927 337" data-label="Text">
<p>Testing where your DNA is compared to one or more family members may be performed. This may help better understand your results or show if your family members have the same variant as you.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 340 847 352" data-label="Text">
<p>Before you sign this consent form, you should speak with your healthcare provider. They can help you understand this testing and what it means for your health.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 362 147 374" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>TEST RESULTS</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 380 411 392" data-label="Text">
<p>There are several types of test results that may be reported including:</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 394 926 516" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li><b>Positive:</b> A variant in the DNA was found that is related to your health issues or a health issue that you are at an increased risk of having in the future. These changes that cause disease are also known as pathogenic variants.</li>
<li><b>Negative:</b> No variants in the DNA were found that are related to your health issues or that would increase your risk of a health issue in the future.</li>
<li><b>Variant of Uncertain Clinical Significance (VUS):</b> A variant in the DNA was found that we do not know its effect, if any, on health. More testing may be needed for you or your family if a VUS is found that may be associated with your health issues.</li>
<li><b>Secondary and Incidental Findings (Optional):</b> Testing can sometimes find a variant in the DNA not related to the reason for testing but can change your medical care. <b>Note:</b> Certain issues within the brain start in adulthood and get worse over time (neurodegenerative). They often have no cure or treatment. By default, these variants will not be reported unless they are related to your health issues. However, variants in one or more of these gene(s) can be requested if needed. Your provider must write each gene needed in your test order.</li>
<li><b>Genes of No Known Disease Association (Optional):</b> Testing may find a variant in a gene that is not known to cause disease. This may be helpful to learn more about these genes in the future. These results do not currently impact medical management or indicate a diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 525 280 537" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>SECONDARY AND INCIDENTAL FINDINGS</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 542 912 564" data-label="Text">
<p>The following categories of variants are not expected to cause your current health issues. However, they can each be requested to be reported. Knowing about these variants might affect your future medical care.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 565 924 601" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li><b>ACMG Secondary Findings:</b> The American College of Medical Genetics and Genomics (ACMG) recommends reporting disease-causing variants in certain genes that cause health issues. Each family member can request this group of variants to be reported.</li>
<li><b>Incidental Findings:</b> Other variants known to cause health issues but that are not causing your current health issues.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 611 259 624" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>CONSIDERATIONS AND LIMITATIONS</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 629 906 742" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>You should speak with your provider before signing this consent form to understand the risks, benefits, and alternatives to testing.</li>
<li>Testing may show you have, or are at increased chance of having, a health issue. It may show that you have an increased chance of having a child with a health issue.</li>
<li>Even if the variant(s) causing your health issues are found, how these issues might progress or improve with treatment might not be known. Affected family members with the same variant might not be affected like you are.</li>
<li>Depending on the results of testing, more testing may be needed to understand these results. This testing might be needed for you and/or other family members.</li>
<li>A negative result does not rule out the chance for health issues. Our knowledge of variants and how they cause disease may change over time as we learn more about genetics. Testing has limitations to what it can find as well.</li>
<li>Certain factors may lead to incorrect results. These include mislabeled samples, incorrect information in the test order, and rare technical errors.</li>
<li>More sample may be needed from you if the first sample is not sufficient to complete testing.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 753 367 765" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>USE OF DATA AND SPECIMEN FOR RESEARCH PURPOSES</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 769 923 809" data-label="Text">
<p>Biological specimens, test results, and associated information may be used by Baylor Genetics and its research partners for anonymous or coded research purposes, including improving genetic testing, advancing knowledge of genetic conditions, and developing new technologies, including inclusion in de-identified clinical databases, only with the patient's informed consent. Patient data and specimen will not be used for anonymous or coded research, unless authorized by marking below. A patient's decision to decline participation shall not affect their ability to receive testing from Baylor Genetics.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 810 600 823" data-label="Text">
<p>For Oregon patients, please consult the state specific consent form found at <a href="http://www.baylorgenetics.com/forms">www.baylorgenetics.com/forms</a>.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 824 497 838" data-label="Text">
<p><input checked="checked" type="checkbox"/> I authoriz e Baylor Genetics the use of my specimen and de-identified data for research.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 848 337 860" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>FOR SAMPLES FROM NEW YORK STATE RESIDENTS</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 863 907 886" data-label="Text">
<p>Samples from New York State residents <u>shall not be included</u> in research without written consent. Samples will not be retained for more than sixty (60) days after receipt by Baylor Genetics, unless authorized by marking below. No tests other than those authorized shall be performed on the samples.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="62 888 803 900" data-label="Text">
<p><input checked="checked" type="checkbox"/> I authorize Baylor Genetics to retain sample(s) longer based on our retention policy for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes.</p>
</div>

<div data-bbox="68 188 354 200" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 206 930 248" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>If several family members are tested, knowing the correct biological relationships among them is important. In rare cases, testing can show that family members are not related as expected. If this is found, we may contact the provider who ordered your testing.</li>
<li>If this testing is requested to be cancelled after the order and sample are sent to the laboratory, please see our Test Cancellation Policy at <a href="http://www.baylorgenomics.com/cancel-test/">www.baylorgenomics.com/cancel-test/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 259 427 271" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>PATIENT CONFIDENTIALITY AND SAMPLE RETENTION (CONTINUED)</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 277 930 458" data-label="List-Group">
<ul>
<li>Only Baylor Genetics and its contracted partners will have access to your sample for the ordered testing. Results from testing will only be released to: (i) a licensed healthcare provider, (ii) those authorized in writing, (iii) the patient or their personal representative, and (iv) those allowed access to test results by law. You have the right to access your test results from Baylor Genetics by providing a written request. You also have the right to request raw data obtained from your sample by providing a written request or HIPAA Authorization Form.</li>
<li>In rare cases, people with genetic diseases may have problems with health insurance and employment. The U.S. Federal Government has several laws that prohibit discrimination based on test results by health insurance companies and employers. These laws also prohibit unauthorized disclosure of this information. For more information, please visit <a href="http://www.genome.gov/10000277">www.genome.gov/10000277</a>.</li>
<li>Samples will be kept in the laboratory based on our retention policy. Once testing is completed, the de-identified sample may be used for test development, quality assurance, and training purposes. Samples are not returned to patients or providers unless requested prior to testing. You and your heirs will not receive payments, benefits, or rights to any resulting products or discoveries.</li>
<li>The information from your testing may be used in scientific research, publications or presentations, but your specific identity will not be revealed. We may contact your provider to obtain more clinical information about you. Baylor Genetics also performs other types of scientific research and may contact you to see if you would like to be involved.</li>
<li>Variants found may be submitted to databases. The medical community uses these databases to collect information about how variants might cause disease to improve testing and treatment for patients. An example is ClinVar, a free, public archive of reports on human genetics. Limited clinical information may need to be shared with these databases. In rare cases, this information may be enough to allow you or your family members to be identified.</li>
<li>For more information on privacy practices at Baylor Genetics, please visit <a href="http://www.baylorgenomics.com/privacy-practices/">www.baylorgenomics.com/privacy-practices/</a>.</li>
</ul>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 469 199 480" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>FINANCIAL AGREEMENT</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 486 928 526" data-label="Text">
<p>By signing below, I hereby authorize Baylor Genetics to provide my insurance carrier any information necessary, including test results, for processing my insurance claim. I understand that I am responsible for any co-pay, co-insurance, and unmet deductible that the insurance policy dictates. I designate Baylor Genetics as my designated representative for purposes of appealing any denial of benefits by my insurance carrier. I irrevocably assign associated payment to Baylor Genetics, and direct that payment be made directly to Baylor Genetics. Please note, some payers may not cover certain screening tests.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 528 928 560" data-label="Text">
<p>If my health insurer does not cover the test or I do not have health insurance, I have received a good faith estimate of the cost for the genetic testing ordered by my provider and agree to pay for the cost of the genetic testing billed to me by Baylor Genetics based on that good faith estimate. More information is available in Baylor Genetics' No Surprises Act and Good Faith Estimate Notice located at <a href="https://www.baylorgenomics.com/no-surprises-act/">https://www.baylorgenomics.com/no-surprises-act/</a>.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 561 643 573" data-label="Text">
<p>A Medicare Advance Beneficiary Notice (ABN) is required for services Medicare identifies as not medically necessary.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="68 583 206 594" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>PATIENT AUTHORIZATION</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="65 600 906 641" data-label="Text">
<p>By signing this statement of consent, I acknowledge that I have read, understand, and hereby grant my informed consent for genetic testing. I have received appropriate explanations from my healthcare provider about the planned genetic test(s) and possible results. I have been informed by my healthcare provider about the availability and importance of genetic counseling and have been provided with written information identifying a genetic counselor or medical geneticist who can provide such counseling services. All my questions have been answered, and I have had the necessary time to make an informed decision about the genetic test(s).</p>
</div>

<div data-bbox="64 188 396 199" data-label="Section-Header">
<p><b>FOR SURROGATES PREGNANCIES - FOR PRENATAL WES ONLY:</b></p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="64 204 929 234" data-label="Text">
<p>Maternal cell contamination (MCC) studies use blood or another sample from a pregnant person. MCC studies are used to determine that the sample being tested belongs to the fetus and not the pregnant person. The results of MCC studies are not used for the treatment or management of the fetus, pregnant person, or other individuals, and are not part of the pregnant person's designated medical record.</p>
</div>
<div data-bbox="64 236 397 250" data-label="Text">

<div data-bbox="63 616 924 780" data-label="Form">
<p><b>G. OPTIONS: Check only one box. We cannot choose a box for you.</b></p>
<p><input checked="" type="checkbox"/> <b>OPTION 1.</b> I want the <b>Baylor Genetics Test</b> listed above. You may ask to be paid now, but I also want Medicare billed for an official decision on payment, which is sent to me on a Medicare Summary Notice (MSN). I understand that if Medicare doesn't pay, I am responsible for payment, but I can appeal to Medicare by following the directions on the MSN. If Medicare does pay, you will refund any payments I made to you, less co-pays or deductibles.</p>
<p><input type="checkbox"/> <b>OPTION 2.</b> I want the <b>Baylor Genetics Test</b> listed above, but do not bill Medicare. You may ask to be paid now as I am responsible for payment. I cannot appeal if Medicare is not billed.</p>
<p><input type="checkbox"/> <b>OPTION 3.</b> I don't want the <b>Baylor Genetics Test</b> listed above. I understand with this choice I am <b>not</b> responsible for payment, and I cannot appeal to see if Medicare would pay.</p>
